Jamison Brereton

64 (776)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Ka┼Ыyapa M─Бr─лca
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
The hymn begins with an insistent tr╠еca establishing Soma as a bull. What follows is for the most part a conventional treatment of the purification process, with special emphasis on his entry into тАЬthe seaтАЭ (that is, the purificatory waters, vss. 8, 16, 17, 19, 27). The association with the Sun found in the preceding hymn is also present here, with Soma not merely yoking the SunтАЩs horse, Eta┼Ыa, but identified with him (vs. 19) and with the Sun himself in the final words of the hymn (vs. 30; see also vss. 7, 9). SomaтАЩs light and brilliance are also mentioned throughout (vss. 1, 8, 13, 15, 28).

Jamison Brereton Notes

61-67 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are the bright sprinkler; you shining (Soma) are the sprinkler whose occupation is sprinkling; you, the sprinkler, sustain the rites (of men and gods).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

A bull are you, Soma, a brilliant oneтАФa bull following his bullish commandments, o god.
As bull, you have established your own foundations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

OldenbergтАЩs interpr. of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б in c as a neut. pl. adj. with dh├бrm─Бс╣Зi seems both unnecessary and unlikely. I know of no other neut. forms of vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- (the few cited by Oldenberg are not convincing), which suggests to me that, despite its widely accepted classification as an adj., the stem is synchronically a masc. noun, which, however, can be used as an adjunct strengthener of another noun, hence тАЬbull XтАЭ as the equivalent of тАЬbullish XтАЭ - a usage similar to English тАШhorseтАЩ as an augmentative, meaning тАШstrong, large, coarseтАЩ (as in, for ex., horseradish). See https://www.etymonline.com/word/horseradish Moreover, since nom. sg.

vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б opens the two previous p─Бdas of this vs., it seems unlikely that a morphologically different, and at the least very rare, phonologically identical form would open the third - esp. since, when a neut. adj. is required in the next vs. (2a), the deriv. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зya- is employed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this opening tс╣Ыca is marked by the identification of Soma and his attributes with a bull (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-). This theme is especially dominant in vss. 1 and 2: all three p─Бdas of vs. 1 open vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б, with the bahuvr─лhi vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-vrataс╕е ending the first hemistich; vs. 2 is even more insistent, with two forms of the stem (or deriv. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зya-) in each of the three p─Бdas. By contrast, vs. 3 only nods at the theme: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б appears once in 3a, though the final word of the vs., vс╣Ыdhi, may be meant to echo the word phonologically.

Soma, thou art a splendid Steer, a Steer, O God, with steerlike sway:
Thou as a Steer ordainest laws.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO sprinkler, the strengh of you the sprinkler consists in sprinkling, your worship consists in sprinkling, your juice consists in sprinkling; you truly are always the sprinkler.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of you, the bull, bullish is the strength; your wooden (cup) is a bull, your exhilarating drink a bull.
In truth, o bull, you are really a bull. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this opening tс╣Ыca is marked by the identification of Soma and his attributes with a bull (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-). This theme is especially dominant in vss. 1 and 2: all three p─Бdas of vs. 1 open vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б, with the bahuvr─лhi vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-vrataс╕е ending the first hemistich; vs. 2 is even more insistent, with two forms of the stem (or deriv. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зya-) in each of the three p─Бdas. By contrast, vs. 3 only nods at the theme: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б appears once in 3a, though the final word of the vs., vс╣Ыdhi, may be meant to echo the word phonologically.

Griffith

Steer-strong thy might is as a steer’s, steerstrong thywood, steer-like thy drink
A Steer indeed, O Steer, art thou.

Geldner

Dein, des Bullen, Kraft ist bullenhaft, bullenhaft ist das Holz, bullenhaft dein Rausch. Wahrhaftig, du bist ein Bulle, o Bulle.

Grassmann

Dir Stier ist eigen Stieres Kraft, ein Stier die Flut, ein Stier der Rausch, Ein rechter Stier bist du, o Stier.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndu, the sprinkler, you nigh like a horse; you give us cattle, you give us horses; open the doors for our wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, the bull, whinny like a horse. Sur(round) the cows, sur(round) the steeds, o drop;
open up the doors for wealth for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted above, the bull theme gets suddenly muted in this vs.; in compensation, as it were, other animals are introduced: a horse (a), cows and steeds (b).

Opinions vary on how to render the first two p─Бdas, in part because of uncertainty about the verb cakradaс╕е. Given the immediately preceding simile ├б┼Ыvo n├б, the verb should be intransitive in the sense тАШroar, whinnyтАЩ; this matches the usage of the simple thematic (aor.?) krada- in passages like IX.97.28 ├б┼Ыvo n├б krado vr╠е╠Бс╣гabhir yuj─Бn├бс╕е тАЬLike a horse you whinny on being yoked by the bulls.тАЭ However, the b p─Бda, s├бс╣Г g─Б╠Бс╕е тАж s├бm ├бrvataс╕е, with two acc. pl.s makes problems. Geldner jury-rigs what we might call a semi-transitive usage of the verb with s├бm, тАЬzusammenbr├╝llenтАЭ (тАШroar [smtg] togetherтАЩ)(see also Ober I.518), while registering the intransitive usage in the simile parenthetically: тАЬWie ein Ross (wiehernd) sollst du, der Bulle, uns Rinder und Rennpferde zusammen br├╝llen (brausen).тАЭ Despite the precarious nature of this solution, it may be the best one available, and I would entertain an alternative tr. тАЬYou the bull roar like a horse, (roaring) together cows and steeds.тАЭ I adopt a similar one in the published translation for the very similar passage IX.90.4 s├бс╣Г cikrado mah├│ asm├бbhyaс╣Г v─Б╠Бj─Бn, with the variant stem cikrada-, also cited by Geldner and Renou, though I am not certain I subscribe to that now (see comm. ad loc.). By contrast, Renou clearly takes cakradaс╕е as a trans./caus. redupl. aor.: тАЬTel un cheval, fais mugir ensemble тАж les vaches тАж ensemble (fais hennir) les coursiers.тАЭ However, the clear intrans. sense of krada- with the simile in the parallel passage cited above speaks against the caus. usage; moreover, as disc. at length in my -├бya-book (110-11), neither cakrada- nor the redupl. aor. cikrada- with apparent тАЬcaus.тАЭ redupl. shows true transitive usage until the late RV; they also seem to be essentially interchangeable.

I have a different solution for this passage (though it wonтАЩt work for IX.90.4): it is of course a commonplace that the preverbs s├бm and v├н form a complementary pair. Here I suggest that the standard lexeme v├н тИЪvс╣Ы тАШuncover, open upтАЩ found in c has given rise situationally to an opposing expression s├бm тИЪvс╣Ы тАШcover, surroundтАЩ in b, with the verb gapped (or rather anticipated: vс╣Ыdhi at the end of c). The bull is urged to deliver cows and horses to us by confining them. The proposed lexeme s├бm тИЪvс╣Ы does marginally exist; see I.121.15, with s├бm тАж varanta in intrans. value, as well as ppl. s├бс╣Гvс╣Ыta- (VIII.17.7). I thus read the verb cakradaс╕е only with p─Бda a.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this opening tс╣Ыca is marked by the identification of Soma and his attributes with a bull (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-). This theme is especially dominant in vss. 1 and 2: all three p─Бdas of vs. 1 open vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б, with the bahuvr─лhi vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa-vrataс╕е ending the first hemistich; vs. 2 is even more insistent, with two forms of the stem (or deriv. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зya-) in each of the three p─Бdas. By contrast, vs. 3 only nods at the theme: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б appears once in 3a, though the final word of the vs., vс╣Ыdhi, may be meant to echo the word phonologically.

Thou, Indu, as a vigorous horse, hast neighed together steeds and kine:
Unbar for us the doors to wealth.

O wiehere gleich wie ein Hengst uns Ross’ und Rinder, Indu, her, Des Reichthums Thore ├╢ffne uns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In addition to the link to vs. 3 just mentioned, p─Бda c contains a clever echo of 2a.

тАЬMay those Soma-juices pour forth for the offerer (of libations) all the treasures of heaven and earth and of the firmament.тАЭ

All goods for the piousтАФheavenly, earthly, and those of the midspaceтАФ let these soma juices bring in purifying themselves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The preverb ─Б╠Бthat turns p├бva- into a quasi-transitive тАЬbring by purifying oneselfтАЭ immediately follows the verb, allowing p├бvant─Бm to take a position matching. that of p├бvante in 5c and p├бvam─Бnasya in 7a.

English translation:

тАЬAll-beholding Soma, your streams as you are being purified are sent forth like the rays of the sun at present.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O you who find [/know] all, of you purifying yourself the surges have surged forth,
like the rays of the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root noun cmpd vi┼Ыva-v├нd-, like other -v├нd- cmpds, is completely ambiguous between тАШknowing allтАЩ and тАШfinding allтАЩ (for vi┼Ыvav├нd- itself see Scarlatta 489 and more generally 480-93). In this context, given SomaтАЩs bestowal of тАЬall goodsтАЭ (v├н┼Ыv─Б тАж v├бsu) in the previous vs. (6a), as well as SomaтАЩs journey to all forms in 8b, тАШall-findingтАЩ seems preferable.

The simile in c, s┼л╠Бryasyeva n├б r├б┼Ыmayaс╕е, is redundantly marked, with adjacent simile particles iva n├б. There is no structural reason for this; it must result from the attempt to fit the simile s┼л╠Бryasyeva ra┼Ыm├бyaс╕е found elsewhere in trimeter verse (see nearby IX.69.6, also I.135.9, V.55.3, X.91.4) into a dimeter line. Or, to be more precise, to accommodate the fact that when a form of s┼л╠Бrya- opens a vs. line, it does not show distraction to s┼л╠Бr i ya-, in order to avoid placing a light syllable in 2nd position. In a dimeter line, in which this simile has to occupy the whole p─Бda, the failure to distract produces a 7-syllable line, and so n├б was presumably added to fill the gap in the line. In a trimeter line that has the simile in initial position (with undistracted s┼л╠Бryasyeva), further material can be added at the end (so I.135.9, IX.69.6), and in a trimeter line where the simile follows the caesura, s┼л╠Бryasyeva can be distracted (so V.55.3, X.91.4) in that position.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, p├бvam─Бnasya in 7a chains with forms to the same stem in vss. 5 and 6. 7b pr├б тАж asс╣Ыkс╣гata also echoes ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata pr├б, which opens the previous tс╣Ыca (4a). The tс╣Ыca is unified by the similes comparing Soma to the Sun in vss. 7 and 9, possibly found also in the beacon (ket├║-) of vs. 8.

English translation:

тАЬSoma, you who are the ocean, bestowing knowledge, have from heaven to all our various forms, and bestow (variouskinds of wealth on us).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Making a beacon, from heaven you rush toward all forms.
O Soma, you swell as the sea.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted above, itтАЩs quite possible, even likely, that the beacon in p─Бda a is a reference to the sun and therefore another assimilation of Soma to the Sun, as is more explicit in vss. 7 and 9. For the association between ket├║- and the sun, cf., e.g., VII.63.2 ket├║с╕е тАж s┼л╠Бryasya. L├╝ders (702) suggests rather that the ket├║- is lightning, without argument.

Geldner renders b as тАЬтАж rinnst du … alle Farben annehmendтАЭ; similar L├╝ders (702) тАЬstr├╢mst du vom Himmel her in alle Erscheinungsformen.тАЭ But the acc. with abh├н тИЪс╣Ыс╣г is always a goal (to choose just one example, cf. nearby IX.62.3 abhy ├аrс╣гanti suс╣гс╣нut├нm тАЬthey rush towards the lovely praise-hymnтАЭ), and I donтАЩt see where (or why) they get their alternative interpr. By my interpr. the тАЬall formsтАЭ to which the soma rushes could be the materials the soma will be mixed with (water, milk), or everything found on the ritual ground, or indeed everything on earth and in the midspace, the тАЬall goodsтАЭ of vs. 6.

07-09 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, p├бvam─Бnasya in 7a chains with forms to the same stem in vss. 5 and 6. 7b pr├б тАж asс╣Ыkс╣гata also echoes ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata pr├б, which opens the previous tс╣Ыca (4a). The tс╣Ыca is unified by the similes comparing Soma to the Sun in vss. 7 and 9, possibly found also in the beacon (ket├║-) of vs. 8.

Griffith

Making the light that shines from heaven thou flowest on to every form
Soma, thou swellest like a sea.

Geldner

Dein Banner aufsteckend rinnst du vom Himmel, alle Farben annehmend. Wie das Meer schwillst du an, o Soma.

Grassmann

Vom Himmel Licht erzeugend str├╢mst du alle Herrlichkeit herbei, Du schwillst, o Soma, als ein Meer.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPurified Soma, when sent forth you utter a cry (when your juice) like the sun god passed through the supporting (filter).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Yourself being impelled, you send out your speech, you who purify yourself at your expansion.
You have roared like the Sun-god.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b, p├бvam─Бna v├нdharmaс╣Зi, is found three times (here, IX.4.9, and IX.100.7) in three different syntactic contexts, so this has to be the constituency: the voc. plus the loc. Renou takes the тАШspeechтАЩ (v─Б╠Бcam) from p─Бda a as the implicit subject of v├нdharmaс╣Зi (тАЬpour quтАЩelle se r├йpande au loinтАЭ), but because speech is lacking in the other occurrences of the p─Бda, this cannot be correct. Most helpful for the interpr. is the fuller expression in IX.86.30 (also adduced by Ober II.152) tv├бm pav├нtre r├бjaso v├нdharmaс╣Зi … pavam─Бna p┼лyase тАЬYou, selfpurifying soma, are purified in the filter, in the spreading expanse of space …,тАЭ where the spread of the soma liquid across the fleece filter is compared to the spread (probably of light) in cosmic space (r├бjas-).

The simile in the third p─Бda, ├бkr─Бn dev├│ n├б s┼л╠Бryaс╕е тАЬyou have roared like the Sungod,тАЭ is abrupt in its imagery, in that roaring is not the first quality we associate with the sun. There are several ways to account for the phraseology. In OldenbergтАЩs view (fld by L├╝ders 258), the shared quality of Soma and Sun is not expressed by the verb, which is independent of the simile. This independence would be comparable to that found in the preceding hymn, IX.63.13, where the same simile (s├│mo dev├│ n├б s┼л╠Бryaс╕е) is found, with a different but equally incompatible verb phrase ├бdribhiс╕е тАж sut├бс╕е тАЬpressed by stones,тАЭ which is certainly not true of the Sun. This is the easiest solution. Geldner (n. 9c) suggests rather that itтАЩs a condensed comparison to the SunтАЩs horse (sim. Ober I.224). In my view, OldenbergтАЩs interpr. is strictly correct, but I think the poet, by juxtaposing the simile with an apparently inappropriate verb, is forcing the striking image of a roaring Sun, which both works as a kind of synaesthesia (the intense brightness of the sun is experienced as intense noise) and imposes a third intermediate term, a horse or bull, to which both the Sun and Soma are compared.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, p├бvam─Бnasya in 7a chains with forms to the same stem in vss. 5 and 6. 7b pr├б тАж asс╣Ыkс╣гata also echoes ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гata pr├б, which opens the previous tс╣Ыca (4a). The tс╣Ыca is unified by the similes comparing Soma to the Sun in vss. 7 and 9, possibly found also in the beacon (ket├║-) of vs. 8.

Griffith

Urged on thou sendest out thy voice, O Pavamana; thou hast moved,
Like the God Surya, to the sieve.

Geldner

Zur Eile getrieben entsendest du die Stimme, o Pavamana, wenn du dich ausbreitest; du hast gewiehert wie der Gott Surya.

Grassmann

Entsandt erhebst du den Gesang, o rieselnder, du wiehertest Am Himmel wie der Sonnengott.

тАЬGreen-tinted (Soma) lauded by hymns,being dropped into the curds and milk and being purified, bestow wealth and food upon the worshipper.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe swift Soma-juices being cleansed (go to) the firmament without an effort; they go to the abode of the water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Continually being groomed, the lively drops
have come at will to the sea, to the womb of truth. с│У

Easily have the living drops, made beautiful, approached the lake,
Yea, to the place of sacrifice.

Die Indu’s, die gereinigten, die schnellen, sind voll Lust zum Meer Gegangen in des Opfers Schooss.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the swift (Soma) takes his plural ce on the golden seat of sacrifice, he abandons (the sacrifice) of the foolish man.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e., he does not approach the sacrifice of those who do not worship; he only approaches the sacrifice of worshippers

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDevoted (worshippers) glorify Soma; the well-disposed desire to sacrifice; the perverse-minded sink (into hell).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The seekers have cried out to (him); the discerning wish to attain (him). The undiscriminating sink down.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ven├б- see comm. ad VIII.100.5.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The undiscerning (├бpracetasaс╕е) in 20c are contrasted with the discerning (pr├бcetasaс╕е 21b) and the undiscriminating (├бvicetasaс╕е 21c). The first vs. (19) of the tс╣Ыca does not participate.

Griffith

The friends have sung in unison, the prudent wish to sacrifice:
Down sink the unintelligent.

Geldner

Die Seher haben ihm zugeschrieen, die Klugen streben ihm zu; die Tore sinken unter.

Grassmann

Die Freunde haben ihn ger├╝hmt, die Weisen opfern ihm mit Lust, Zu Grunde geht der Thoren Schar.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The mention of the divine recipients of the soma in vss. 22 and 24 marks this tс╣Ыca, though the middle vs. lacks this feature. The (human) inspired poets (v├нpr─Бс╕е) in 23 implicitly contrast with the kav├н- Soma, addressed in the voc. in 24. Note also that this is the third tс╣Ыca in a row that refers to sitting on (or coming to) тАЬthe womb of truthтАЭ (17c, 20ab, 22c), a trope found also in 11c; all four expressions are slightly different, though containing the same basic elements: 11c s─л╠Бdann с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Б╠Б, 17c ├бgmann с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Б╠Б, 20ab ─Б╠БтАж y├│niс╣Г hiraс╣Зy├бyam тАж с╣Ыt├бsya s─л╠Бdati, 22c с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Бs├бdam. For further on this trope see comm. ad vs. 30 below.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The mention of the divine recipients of the soma in vss. 22 and 24 marks this tс╣Ыca, though the middle vs. lacks this feature. The (human) inspired poets (v├нpr─Бс╕е) in 23 implicitly contrast with the kav├н- Soma, addressed in the voc. in 24. Note also that this is the third tс╣Ыca in a row that refers to sitting on (or coming to) тАЬthe womb of truthтАЭ (17c, 20ab, 22c), a trope found also in 11c; all four expressions are slightly different, though containing the same basic elements: 11c s─л╠Бdann с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Б╠Б, 17c ├бgmann с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Б╠Б, 20ab ─Б╠БтАж y├│niс╣Г hiraс╣Зy├бyam тАж с╣Ыt├бsya s─л╠Бdati, 22c с╣Ыt├бsya y├│nim ─Бs├бdam. For further on this trope see comm. ad vs. 30 below.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unusual acc. expression v─Б╠Бcam тАж sah├бsrabharс╣Зasam is found in both 25 and 26 (in different order). For sah├бsra-bharс╣Зas- see comm. ad IX.60.2. All three vss.

contain the nom. sg. masc. pun─Бn├бс╕е.

Griffith

Yea, Soma, Indu, while thou art purified do thou bring to us
Speech thousandfold that longs for war.

Geldner

Und bring uns die Tausend aufwiegende Rede, o Soma, die Belohnung erwartende, wenn du dich l├дuterst, Soma!

Grassmann

Das Lied, was tausend Gaben beut, o Soma, den Triumphgesang, Bring’, Indu, her, gereinigter!

Jamison Brereton

(Provided) with ever-flashing light, with a form that encircles with chant are (both) the clear soma drinks and those mixed with cows [=milk].

Jamison Brereton Notes

On pari тИЪstubh see nearby IX.62.24. It is not entirely clear to me how the kс╣Ы╠Бp- (form, body) of Soma would тАШencircle with chant/rhythmтАЩ, since its physical form should not be producing noise. More common is the association of kс╣Ы╠Бp- with light (esp. the light of Agni), as Renou points out (cf. VI.2.6 kс╣Ыp─Б╠БтАж rocase, VII.3.9 sv├бy─Б kс╣Ыp─Б╠Бtanv─Б╠Аr├│cam─Бnaс╕е), but in our passage ruc─Б╠Бand kс╣Ыp─Б╠Бare parallel and independent. A passive sense тАШencircled with chant/rhythmтАЩ (so Renou) would work better in context, but that seems precluded by the use of the act. stem st├│bha-.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe powerful Soma urged by the urging (worshippers) goes collected to the battle like warriors entering (the battle-field).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

To the battle: metaphorically, for sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Being impelled, guided by the impellers, the prize-seeker has stridden to the prizeтАФ
sitting (on the womb of truth) like raptor(-birds).

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a contains what appears to be an etymological figure, but I consider it somewhat trickier than that. The first two word, hinv─Бn├│ hetс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е, are transparently related and easy to construe together, and IX.13.6 hiy─Бn─Б╠Бn├б hetс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАЬlike (horses) being driven by their driversтАЭ displays the same apparent configuration. However, the instr. in our passage is followed by a ppl. yat├бс╕е тАШheld, guidedтАЩ, which is regularly preceded by an instr. agent, often nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е (approx. 10x in IX), or in this very hymn, vs. 15 v─Бj├нbhir yat├бс╕е тАЬguided by the prizeseekers.тАЭ So I suggest that hetс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е is actually the agent for following yat├бс╕е, though also adjacent to its etymological kin - a fine twist on the RVic poetic trick of positioning a word between two words both of which it could be (or indeed is) connected to. A more literal rendering of the p─Бda would be тАЬ “… impelled, by the impellers held.тАЭ The simile in c is problematic for several reasons. To begin with, the subject of ab is singular, but the simile must be couched in the plural, given the pres. part. s─л╠Бdantaс╕е. This is less of a problem than it appears: first, this hymn and soma hymns in general regularly switch back and forth between sg. (soma) and pl. (soma drinks / drops, etc.) referring to the same substance, and this could easily be a unmarked case of that. Moreover, if the target of the simile is in the pl., it can have attracted the participle into the pl.

This raises the question: what is soma being compared to? and the related but more technical question: is van├║с╣гaс╕е nom. pl. (and therefore the simile target) or some other case (acc. pl., abl./gen. sg.)? Because we need something to license the pl. of s─л╠Бdantaс╕е and because we need something to compare the soma to, taking van├║с╣гaс╕е as nom. pl. seems the most economical solution - although this requires discounting the attractive parallel adduced by Geldner, I.26.3 s─л╠Бdantu m├бnuс╣гo yath─Б. In that passage m├бnuс╣гaс╕е, which rhymes with our van├║с╣гaс╕е, is gen. sg. (and the pl. impv. s─л╠Бdantu simply agrees with the pl. subject in ab).

That van├║с╣гaс╕е is nom. pl. is also the judgment of Geldner and Renou, though with vastly different semantics. Geldner тАЬwie die wetteifernden Reiter(?)тАЭ (I have no idea where he gets the тАЬriders,тАЭ and his question mark shows his uncertainty about it; nonetheless it was taken up by Ober [II.245] as evidence for horseback riding in the RV!); Renou тАЬ(sтАЩasseyant au s├йjour du с╣Ъta) comme les d├йvots qui sтАЩ(y) asseoient.тАЭ Renou seems closer to the mark, though still pretty far from it. Because of the repetition noted above (ad 22-24) of the trope тАЬsit on the womb of truthтАЭ (4x in this hymn), it seems likely that s─л╠Бdant- here would evoke this recurrent expression, which is certainly appropriate to the soma (drinks) that are the subject of the simile. It is more difficult to identify who or what van├║с╣гaс╕е refers to. This stem, and the associated denom. verb, can have both positive and negative values, expressing various types of eagerness and craving: тАЬstriving, eager, zealous, etc.тАЭ on the one hand (hence RenouтАЩs d├йvots), тАЬover-zealous, covetous, rapacious, etc.тАЭ on the other. Before identifying its usage in this particular passage, IтАЩd like to introduce a third term into the simile. In similes involving sitting, the comparandum is often a bird - e.g., ┼Ыyen├бс╕е in nearby IX.61.21 =

Jamison Brereton Notes

The contrast between the two types of soma drinks, pure and mixed with milk, are highlighted in this tс╣Ыca, at least in my view: 28c s├│m─Бс╕е ┼Ыukr─Б╠Бg├бv─Б┼Ыiraс╕е describes them straightforwardly, while 30ab с╣Ыdh├бk тАж saс╣Гjagm─Бn├бс╕е тАЬseparately (and) uniting (with milk)тАЭ is more cryptic.

Griffith

Led by his drivers, and sent forth, the Strong Steed hath come nigh for spoil,
Like warriors when they stand arrayed.

Geldner

Von den Treibern getrieben, gelenkt ist der Preisrenner nach dem Siegerpreis gelaufen wie die wetteifernden Reiter.

Grassmann

Gespornt von Treibern und gelenkt hat nun der Renner Preis erlangt Wie Krieger sitzend nach dem Streit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSoma, who are a sage mighty and prospering approaching flow from heaven for our prosperity and view.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S┼лryaс╕е is separated from dс╣Ы┼Ыe and explained as suv─лryaс╕е;

с╣Ъdhak = pс╣Ыthak, also used to mean ‘prospering’ (Nirukta 4.25)

Jamison Brereton

Separately [=unmixed], o Soma, and uniting (with milk), as poet of heaven
purify yourself for well-being and as the sun to be seen.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated above (ad 28-30), I believe that the unmixed and mixed soma drinks are referred to here, though no interpr. I know of shares this opinion. The adv. с╣Ы╠Бdhak (so accented) means тАШseparately, apartтАЩ; the form с╣Ыdh├бk with final accent is found only here, and it is difficult to assess what the accentual difference means: is it just a mistake or meaningless variant? or is it meant to signal some change in grammatical function or meaning? If we can fancifully imagine an internal derivation of adverbs quasi-parallel to that of br├бhman- ├а brahm├бn-, y├б┼Ыas- ├а ya┼Ы├бs-, perhaps с╣Ыdh├бk refers to something characterized by separateness. With a further flight of fancy, we can suggest that this would be the unmixed soma, referred to unequivocally two vss. earlier as ┼Ыukr├б- (28c), and contrasting with the soma that тАЬunitesтАЭ (saс╣Гjagm─Бn├б-) with milk, again straightforwardly referred to in 28c as g├бv─Б┼Ыir-. Although neither of the terms in vs. 30 is elsewhere used of a type of soma, at least as far as I know, the contrastive pairing was set up at the beginning of the tс╣Ыca and could, I would assert, have been decoded by a RVic audience and applied to the more opaque expressions here. I will not discuss the alternative interpr. (Geldner, Renou, L├╝ders 259, Ober I.457, II.143), which differ wildly from mine and from each other and, in the case of Geldner and Renou, depend on an out-of-date interpr. of с╣Ы╠Бdhak.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The contrast between the two types of soma drinks, pure and mixed with milk, are highlighted in this tс╣Ыca, at least in my view: 28c s├│m─Бс╕е ┼Ыukr─Б╠Бg├бv─Б┼Ыiraс╕е describes them straightforwardly, while 30ab с╣Ыdh├бk тАж saс╣Гjagm─Бn├бс╕е тАЬseparately (and) uniting (with milk)тАЭ is more cryptic.

Griffith

Specially, Soma, coming as a Sage from heaven to prosper us,
Flow like the Sun for us to see.
